* Successful bronchoscopic microwave ablation of [TARGET 1] RUL posterior segment nodule with post-ablation CBCT showing expected ground-glass halo.
* CXR in PACU; CT chest at ~4–6 weeks to assess ablation zone.
* Standard post-bronchoscopy precautions; call for fever, hemoptysis > tablespoon, worsening dyspnea.

PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: R91.1 (solitary pulmonary nodule), suspected early-stage lung cancer
POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: Same

PROCEDURES:

* Robotic navigational bronchoscopy to RUL lesion
* Radial EBUS confirmation (eccentric)
* TBNA + transbronchial biopsy for diagnosis
* Microwave ablation of pulmonary nodule (bronchoscopic) 32998-?? (descriptor line wrapped)
* Cone-beam CT (CBCT) spin for tool-in-lesion confirmation

ANESTHESIA: General anesthesia (ETT)
EBL: Minimal
COMPLICATIONS: None

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
After informed consent, [PATIENT] (67-year-old male) was brought to the hybrid suite. Airway inspection with flexible bronchoscopy revealed no endobronchial lesions. Robotic platform was docked and navigation performed to the RUL posterior segment target based on pre-op CT plan. Radial EBUS demonstrated an eccentric lesion; fluoroscopy and CBCT confirmed tool-in-lesion. TBNA and TBBx were obtained prior to ablation.

A microwave ablation catheter was advanced to the target and energy delivered in staged applications with repositioning for margin coverage. Repeat CBCT showed expected ablation change without pneumothorax. Bronchial toileting performed; hemostasis confirmed. Patient extubated in stable condition.
SPECIMENS:

* RUL target: TBNA x4 passes
* RUL target: TBBx x6 fragments

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EDGE_CASE_TAGS: extreme_length, inconsistent_formatting
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS:

* R91.1 solitary pulmonary nodule, LLL superior segment (1.8 cm)
* Prior lung surgery; limited reserve

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: Same

PROCEDURES:

1. Flexible bronchoscopy with airway survey
2. Robotic navigation to LLL superior segment target
3. Radial EBUS localization
4. CBCT guidance (spin x2)
5. Diagnostic sampling (TBNA + TBBx)
6. Bronchoscopic microwave ablation of pulmonary nodule

ANESTHESIA: General (ETT)
EBL: ~25 mL
COMPLICATIONS: None

INDICATION:
[PATIENT] is a 76-year-old male with an enlarging LLL superior segment nodule. Tumor board recommended bronchoscopic biopsy with same-session ablation if localization adequate.

DETAILS:
Airway survey without endobronchial lesion. Robotic system docked; navigation performed. Radial EBUS initially eccentric with adjacent atelectasis; catheter manipulated to improve lesion engagement. CBCT spin #1 showed edge position; catheter advanced and angulated slightly; CBCT spin #2 confirmed improved tool-in-lesion.

TBNA x3 passes performed. Forceps biopsies obtained x6. Moderate bleeding occurred after the final biopsy, controlled with suction, iced saline, and brief balloon occlusion in the segment. Hemostasis confirmed.

Microwave ablation catheter advanced; staged applications delivered. Small amount of airway soot/char seen at catheter tip (expected), cleared with suction; no airway injury appreciated. Final bronchoscopy clear; exit imaging without pneumothorax.

SPECIMENS:

* LLL SS nodule: TBNA x3
* LLL SS nodule: TBBx x6
  PLAN:
* CXR in PACU
* CT chest at 6 weeks

STATUS: SUCCESS

================================================================================
NOTE: note_005
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EDGE_CASE_TAGS: extreme_length, reordered_sections
PATIENT CONTEXT:
[PATIENT] is a 64-year-old female with COPD and a peripheral RLL basilar segment nodule (1.6 cm) with interval growth and PET avidity. She is not an ideal surgical candidate. Plan: same-session diagnostic sampling and cryoablation if safe localization achieved.

PLAN / RECOMMENDATIONS (placed first intentionally):

1. Observe in PACU with CXR at 0 and 3 hours.
2. Resume usual inhalers; hold anticoagulation x24h if applicable.
3. CT chest in 4–6 weeks, then 3 months to evaluate involution of ablation zone.
4. Pathology follow-up; oncology referral if malignancy confirmed.

PRE-PROCEDURE DX: R91.1; suspected early-stage NSCLC
POST-PROCEDURE DX: Same

PROCEDURES:

* Robotic bronchoscopy with peripheral navigation
* Radial EBUS localization
* Cone-beam CT confirmation x2
* Transbronchial cryobiopsy (diagnostic)
* Bronchoscopic cryoablation of pulmonary nodule (non-resectional therapy)

ANESTHESIA: General anesthesia (ETT)
AIRWAY DEVICE: 8.0 ETT
EBL: Minimal
COMPLICATIONS: None

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
After consent and time-out, flexible bronchoscopy demonstrated normal tracheobronchial anatomy without endobronchial mass. A robotic system was docked. Navigation was performed to the RLL basilar segment target. Radial EBUS showed an eccentric lesion with adjacent vessel excluded by Doppler on linear EBUS from a segmental takeoff.

CBCT spin #1 confirmed near-lesion position; catheter adjusted. CBCT spin #2 confirmed tool-in-lesion. Diagnostic sampling performed first: TBNA from within the lesion, followed by transbronchial cryobiopsy using a 1.1 mm cryoprobe with balloon occlusion in the segment for hemostasis readiness.

Following diagnostic sampling, cryoablation catheter was positioned centrally within the target. A freeze-thaw-freeze sequence was performed with slight catheter retraction between cycles to broaden coverage. Final CBCT demonstrated expected perilesional ground-glass change. No pneumothorax seen on exit imaging. Airway toileting performed; no active bleeding at conclusion.

SPECIMENS:

* RLL basilar segment nodule: TBNA x4 passes
* RLL basilar segment nodule: cryobiopsy x3

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EDGE_CASE_TAGS: reordered_sections, extreme_length
IMPRESSION / PLAN (front-loaded):

* Bronchoscopic RFA ablation of RLL lateral basilar nodule completed with expected post-ablation CBCT changes.
* No pneumothorax on exit spin; routine post-procedure imaging ordered.
* Follow-up CT chest at ~6 weeks; consider repeat CT at 3 months if equivocal.

PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS:

* R91.1 solitary pulmonary nodule, RLL lateral basilar (1.7 cm)
* Severe COPD, high surgical risk

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: Same

PROCEDURES:

1. Flexible bronchoscopy with airway survey
2. Robotic navigational bronchoscopy to RLL target
3. Radial EBUS localization
4. CBCT guidance (spin x2)
5. Transbronchial needle aspiration + forceps biopsy
6. Bronchoscopic radiofrequency ablation (RFA) of pulmonary nodule (non-thermal planning margins documented)

ANESTHESIA: General anesthesia (ETT)
EBL: ~20 mL
COMPLICATIONS: None

DETAILS:
[PATIENT] is a 74-year-old male with a growing peripheral RLL nodule. Airway exam showed mild secretions, suctioned. Robotic system docked; navigation performed along planned pathway. Radial EBUS demonstrated eccentric lesion; catheter adjusted until near-concentric. CBCT spin #1 suggested edge position; catheter advanced 5–8 mm and repeat CBCT confirmed improved tool-in-lesion.

Sampling obtained prior to ablation (TBNA x3, TBBx x6). Mild bleeding after forceps biopsy controlled with suction and topical iced saline; no balloon occlusion required.

RFA catheter placed centrally. Two overlapping ablations delivered with slight retraction between applications to cover expected margin. Final bronchoscopy showed no active bleeding. Exit CBCT without pneumothorax.

SPECIMENS:

* RLL lateral basilar nodule: TBNA x3 passes
* RLL lateral basilar nodule: TBBx x6 fragments

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EDGE_CASE_TAGS: extreme_length, inconsistent_formatting
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS:

* R91.1 solitary pulmonary nodule, LUL anterior segment
* High surgical risk (poor reserve)

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: Same

PROCEDURES PERFORMED:
A. Robotic bronchoscopy with computer-assisted navigation
B. Radial EBUS localization
C. Cone-beam CT confirmation (pre and post ablation)
D. Transbronchial needle aspiration + forceps biopsy
E. Bronchoscopic microwave ablation of pulmonary nodule
F. BAL (left upper lobe)

ANESTHESIA: General anesthesia
EBL: ~15 mL
COMPLICATIONS: None

INDICATION / HISTORY:
[PATIENT] is a 69-year-old male with emphysema and a growing LUL anterior segment nodule. Multidisciplinary tumor board recommended bronchoscopic diagnosis with the option for same-session ablation.

FINDINGS:

* Airways: mild anthracosis; no endobronchial lesion.
* Radial EBUS: concentric lesion, surrounding aerated lung.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
After consent and time-out, bronchoscopy performed. Robotic system docked and pathway followed to the LUL target. Radial EBUS demonstrated concentric view; CBCT confirmed tool-in-lesion. TBNA x3 performed followed by forceps biopsy. BAL performed.

Microwave ablation catheter advanced and energy delivered with a central application followed by a slight anterior reposition to cover the expected margin. Intermittent suctioning performed; minor oozing resolved spontaneously. Exit CBCT showed expected ablation halo without pneumothorax. Patient extubated and transported to PACU stable.

SPECIMENS:

* LUL nodule: TBNA x3
* LUL nodule: TBBx x6
* BAL: LUL (50 mL instilled; 18 mL return)
  PLAN:
* CXR in PACU
* CT chest at 6 weeks
* Pathology follow-up and oncology referral if indicated

IMPRESSION:
Successful PEF ablation of RLL superior segment nodule without immediate complication.

PLAN:

* CXR in PACU; discharge if stable after observation.
* CT chest 4–6 weeks to assess ablation zone; additional CT at 3 months if indeterminate.
* Hold anticoagulation x24h if applicable.

PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: R91.1 solitary pulmonary nodule, RLL superior segment
POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: Same

PROCEDURES:

* Robotic navigational bronchoscopy to RLL superior segment target
* Radial EBUS localization
* Cone-beam CT guidance (two spins)
* Bronchoscopic cryoablation of pulmonary nodule 32994-?? (line wrapped)

ANESTHESIA: General anesthesia (ETT)
EBL: Minimal
COMPLICATIONS: None

DETAILS:
[PATIENT] is a 59-year-old male with a growing RLL superior segment nodule. Flexible bronchoscopy showed no endobronchial lesion. Navigation performed to the planned target; radial EBUS showed concentric view. CBCT spin confirmed tool-in-lesion; catheter repositioned slightly to improve centrality, then repeat CBCT confirmed. Cryoablation performed with freeze-thaw-freeze sequence with minor catheter pullback to broaden margins. Final airway inspection without bleeding. Exit imaging without PTX.

SPECIMENS: None (prior diagnostic tissue available).
